## Claude
<thinking>
Now I can see the progress clearly. The issue:

1. T1-T4 all passed (HTTP server, delegation, sub-agent tab creation) ✅
2. T5: Claude Handshake FAILED - no "Claude Handshake" log found in 25s
3. No session ID captured
4. Completion never arrived

The problem is clear: Claude CLI is being launched in the sub-agent tab (`claudeTerm.write('claude --dangerously-skip-permissions\r')`), but the handshake state machine never fires. This means Claude isn't starting properly, or the ⏵ prompt isn't appearing, or the detection isn't working.


I'm tracing through the handshake flow: the state machine initializes with WAITING_PROMPT and stores the prompt, then the onData handler should detect the ⏵ or > prompt character and transition to DEBOUNCE_PROMPT, which triggers the log message. But that transition never happens, so either the prompt character isn't being received or the state machine isn't wired up correctly for that tab. I'm realizing the issue might be with the working directory lookup — when a sub-agent tab is created in one project but the delegation references a tab from a different project, the workspace lookup fails and the CWD defaults to an empty string or incorrect path. back to `workspace?.projectPath`.

In the test:
- `activeProjectId` might not match the project that contains the geminiTabId 
- Or the workspace might have a strange projectPath

Actually, looking at the log: `Sub-agent in store: g-tab-10` and `parentTabId: VzdHM=-tab-0`. The `VzdHM=-tab-0` is the truncated version of `L1VzZXJzL2ZlZG9yL0Rlc2t0b3AvY3VzdG9tLXRlcm1pbmFsL3J1bnRpbWUtdGVzdHM=-tab-0` — this is the runtime-tests project's first tab.

But the active tab at the time of setting commandType was `cvfvsg-tab-7`. The real problem is that the fallback PID matching with ppid=0 grabs the first terminal from the `terminals` Map, which happens to be from the runtime-tests project, while the test set up commandType='gemini' on a completely different project's tab. So when `mcp:create-sub-agent-tab` fires with `geminiTabId = VzdHM=-tab-0`, the renderer gets an activeProjectId that doesn't align with where the command was actually set. I see the issue now — the CWD being passed to the sub-agent tab is `__unset__new_project_...`, which isn't a valid path at all. This looks like a state initialization problem where the workspace path isn't being set correctly. When `geminiTab` can't be found because it's from a different project, and the workspace path is empty or undefined, the tab gets created with an invalid working directory, which would cause the Claude process to fail to start.

Looking at the session restore logic, there's a saved `claude-sub` tab with `wasInterrupted: true` that might be interfering with the initialization...

Actually, the real issue is that the handshake log never appeared at all. The onData handler should be checking for the prompt detection and logging `[Claude Handshake] Tab ${tabId}: Prompt detected.`, but that's not showing up in the output, which suggests the Claude process either didn't start or the handshake state machine never triggered.

Looking at the launcher code, it strips the CLAUDECODE environment variable to prevent nested Claude invocations, but that shouldn't prevent Claude CLI from running. The `--dangerously-skip-permissions` flag should still work. So the issue might be that the `claude` binary isn't available in the test environment's PATH, the working directory is invalid, or something else is preventing the process from starting in the first place. Looking at the delegateToClaudeSubAgent function, I see it waits for the renderer to create a tab and send back the tabId, then immediately tries to retrieve the terminal from the store. But there's a potential race condition here — the `createTab` call triggers a `terminal:create` IPC that might not have completed synchronously before we try to access the terminal.

Let me trace through the flow more carefully: the renderer generates a tabId, invokes `terminal:create` with that tabId, the main process creates the PTY and stores it, then returns. The renderer should then send `mcp:sub-agent-tab-created` with the same tabId. So the IDs should match and the terminal should exist by the time we look it up.

I'm going in circles trying to reason through this — I need to add logging to the main process during a test run to see what's actually happening with the tabIds and terminal creation.

The best approach is to add a diagnostic step after the delegation request: wait a moment for the async sub-agent tab creation to complete, then dump all main process logs so I can see if there are any errors or mismatches in the terminal setup. I should also add a custom log filter to focus on MCP and Claude-related lines. Let me update the test to include this.
</thinking>

```
/**
 * Test: MCP Delegation — Gemini → Claude Sub-Agent
 * [E2E+Claude] — Requires live `claude` CLI
 *
 * Запуск: node auto/sandbox/test-mcp-delegate.js
 */

const { launch, waitForTerminal, waitForMainProcessLog, findInLogs } = require('../core/launcher')
const electron = require('../core/electron')
const http = require('http')
const fs = require('fs')
const path = require('path')

// ─── Hard kill at 150s ───
const GLOBAL_MS = 150000
const globalTimer = setTimeout(() => {
  console.error('\n\x1b[31m[KILL] 150s global timeout\x1b[0m')
  process.exit(2)
}, GLOBAL_MS)
globalTimer.unref()

// ─── Logging ───
const c = { R: '\x1b[0m', G: '\x1b[32m', F: '\x1b[31m', C: '\x1b[36m', Y: '\x1b[33m', D: '\x1b[2m' }
const ts = () => new Date().toISOString().slice(11, 19)
const log = {
  step: (m) => console.log(`${c.C}[${ts()}][STEP]${c.R} ${m}`),
  pass: (m) => console.log(`${c.G}[${ts()}][PASS]${c.R} ${m}`),
  fail: (m) => console.log(`${c.F}[${ts()}][FAIL]${c.R} ${m}`),
  warn: (m) => console.log(`${c.Y}[${ts()}][WARN]${c.R} ${m}`),
  info: (m) => console.log(`${c.D}[${ts()}][INFO]${c.R} ${m}`)
}

let passed = 0, failed = 0
function assert(cond, msg) {
  if (cond) { log.pass(msg); passed++ }
  else { log.fail(msg); failed++ }
}

async function withTimeout(promise, ms, label) {
  let timer
  const to = new Promise((_, rej) => { timer = setTimeout(() => rej(new Error(`TIMEOUT ${ms}ms`)), ms) })
  try {
    const r = await Promise.race([promise, to])
    clearTimeout(timer)
    return r
  } catch (err) {
    clearTimeout(timer)
    log.fail(`${label}: ${err.message}`)
    failed++
    return null
  }
}

const MCP_PORT_FILE = path.join(require('os').homedir(), '.noted-terminal', 'mcp-port')

function httpReq(method, url, body) {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const u = new URL(url)
    const req = http.request({
      hostname: u.hostname, port: u.port, path: u.pathname,
      method, timeout: 10000,
      headers: body ? { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' } : {}
    }, (res) => {
      let d = ''
      res.on('data', c => { d += c })
      res.on('end', () => {
        try { resolve({ status: res.statusCode, body: JSON.parse(d) }) }
        catch { resolve({ status: res.statusCode, body: { raw: d } }) }
      })
    })
    req.on('timeout', () => { req.destroy(); reject(new Error('HTTP timeout')) })
    req.on('error', reject)
    if (body) req.write(JSON.stringify(body))
    req.end()
  })
}

// Filter: only MCP / Claude / Handshake / PTY-related main process lines
const MCP_FILTER = /MCP|Handshake|sub.agent|Sub.agent|delegate|claudeState|WAITING_PROMPT|PTY:CREATED|terminal:create|Prompt detect|Sniper|session-detect|Bridge/i

async function main() {
  let app = null

  try {
    // ─── LAUNCH ───
    log.step('Launching Electron...')

    const launched = await withTimeout(
      launch({ logConsole: false, logMainProcess: false, waitForReady: 4000 }),
      25000, 'Electron launch'
    )
    if (!launched) { process.exit(1) }

    app = launched.app
    const { page, mainProcessLogs } = launched

    // Stream MCP-related main process lines in real-time
    let lastLogIdx = 0
    const logPump = setInterval(() => {
      for (let i = lastLogIdx; i < mainProcessLogs.length; i++) {
        if (MCP_FILTER.test(mainProcessLogs[i])) {
          console.log(`${c.D}  [main] ${mainProcessLogs[i].replace(/^\[(stdout|stderr)\]\s*/, '').trim().slice(0, 120)}${c.R}`)
        }
      }
      lastLogIdx = mainProcessLogs.length
    }, 500)

    log.pass('App launched')

    // ─── TERMINAL ───
    log.step('Waiting for terminal...')
    const term = await withTimeout(waitForTerminal(page, 15000), 20000, 'Terminal appear')
    if (!term) { process.exit(1) }
    log.pass('Terminal visible')

    await electron.focusWindow(app)
    await page.waitForTimeout(500)

    // ═══════ T1: MCP HTTP server ═══════
    log.step('T1: MCP HTTP server')
    const portLog = await withTimeout(
      waitForMainProcessLog(mainProcessLogs, '[MCP:HTTP] Server listening', 10000),
      12000, 'MCP HTTP port log'
    )
    assert(!!portLog, 'HTTP server started')

    let mcpPort = null
    try { mcpPort = parseInt(fs.readFileSync(MCP_PORT_FILE, 'utf-8').trim()) } catch {}
    assert(mcpPort > 0, `Port=${mcpPort}`)
    if (!mcpPort) { process.exit(1) }

    const health = await withTimeout(httpReq('GET', `http://127.0.0.1:${mcpPort}/status/xxx`), 5000, 'Health')
    assert(health?.status === 404, 'Health OK')

    // ═══════ T2: Gemini tab ═══════
    log.step('T2: Set commandType=gemini on active tab')
    const tabInfo = await page.evaluate(() => {
      const s = window.useWorkspaceStore?.getState?.()
      const p = s?.openProjects?.get?.(s?.activeProjectId)
      const t = p?.tabs?.get?.(p?.activeTabId)
      return { pid: s?.activeProjectId, tid: p?.activeTabId, cwd: t?.cwd }
    })
    log.info(`Active tab: ${tabInfo.tid} cwd: ${tabInfo.cwd}`)

    await page.evaluate(() => {
      const s = window.useWorkspaceStore?.getState?.()
      const p = s?.openProjects?.get?.(s?.activeProjectId)
      if (p?.activeTabId) s.setTabCommandType(p.activeTabId, 'gemini')
    })
    assert(true, 'commandType set')

    // ═══════ T3: POST /delegate ═══════
    log.step('T3: POST /delegate')
    const resp = await withTimeout(
      httpReq('POST', `http://127.0.0.1:${mcpPort}/delegate`, {
        prompt: 'Say exactly this one word: MCP_TEST_OK',
        ppid: 0
      }),
      10000, 'POST /delegate'
    )
    assert(resp?.status === 200, `HTTP 200 (got ${resp?.status})`)
    const taskId = resp?.body?.taskId
    assert(!!taskId, `taskId: ${taskId?.slice(0, 8)}...`)
    if (!taskId) { process.exit(1) }

    // ═══════ T4: Sub-agent tab ═══════
    log.step('T4: Sub-agent tab creation')
    const createLog = await withTimeout(
      waitForMainProcessLog(mainProcessLogs, 'Claude sub-agent tab created', 15000),
      18000, 'Sub-agent creation log'
    )
    assert(!!createLog, 'Sub-agent tab created')

    // Verify in store
    const saHandle = await withTimeout(
      page.waitForFunction(() => {
        const s = window.useWorkspaceStore?.getState?.()
        if (!s) return null
        for (const [, ws] of s.openProjects) {
          for (const [, t] of ws.tabs) {
            if (t.parentTabId) return { id: t.id, pt: t.parentTabId, ct: t.commandType }
          }
        }
        return null
      }, { timeout: 10000 }),
      12000, 'Store: parentTabId'
    )
    const sa = saHandle ? await saHandle.jsonValue() : null
    assert(!!sa, `Sub-agent in store: ${sa?.id || 'N/A'}`)

    // ═══════ T5: Handshake (Claude start + prompt detection) ═══════
    log.step('T5: Claude handshake (watch for PTY output)')
    log.info('Claude should start in sub-agent PTY and show ⏵ prompt...')

    // Check if claude was written to the terminal
    const claudeLaunchLog = await withTimeout(
      waitForMainProcessLog(mainProcessLogs, 'claude --dangerously-skip-permissions', 5000),
      8000, 'Claude launch command in PTY'
    )
    if (claudeLaunchLog) {
      log.pass('Claude command sent to PTY')
    } else {
      log.warn('Claude command not visible in logs (may still work)')
    }

    // Wait for handshake prompt detection
    const hsLog = await withTimeout(
      waitForMainProcessLog(mainProcessLogs, 'Prompt detected', 45000),
      48000, 'Handshake prompt detection'
    )
    if (hsLog) {
      log.pass(`Handshake: ${hsLog.slice(0, 80)}`)
    } else {
      log.fail('Handshake: no prompt detected')
      // Diagnostic: dump sub-agent PTY tab info
      log.warn('Diagnosing...')
      const diag = await page.evaluate(() => {
        const s = window.useWorkspaceStore?.getState?.()
        const result = []
        for (const [, ws] of s?.openProjects || new Map()) {
          for (const [, t] of ws.tabs) {
            if (t.parentTabId || t.commandType === 'claude') {
              result.push({ id: t.id, cwd: t.cwd, ct: t.commandType, sid: t.claudeSessionId, pt: t.parentTabId })
            }
          }
        }
        return result
      })
      diag.forEach(d => log.info(`  Tab: ${JSON.stringify(d)}`))
    }

    // Session ID
    if (sa) {
      log.info('Waiting for claudeSessionId (30s)...')
      const sidH = await withTimeout(
        page.waitForFunction((subId) => {
          const s = window.useWorkspaceStore?.getState?.()
          for (const [, ws] of s?.openProjects || new Map()) {
            const t = ws.tabs?.get?.(subId)
            if (t?.claudeSessionId?.length > 10) return t.claudeSessionId
          }
          return null
        }, sa.id, { timeout: 30000 }),
        32000, 'Session ID'
      )
      const sid = sidH ? await sidH.jsonValue() : null
      if (sid) log.pass(`SessionID: ${sid.slice(0, 20)}...`)
      else log.warn('SessionID not captured (continuing anyway)')
    }

    // ═══════ T6: Completion ═══════
    log.step('T6: Completion (wait for [MCPResult])')
    let dots = 0
    const hb = setInterval(() => { dots++; log.info(`Waiting... ${dots * 10}s`) }, 10000)

    const completeLog = await withTimeout(
      waitForMainProcessLog(mainProcessLogs, '[MCPResult]', 60000, 500),
      65000, '[MCPResult]'
    )
    clearInterval(hb)
    assert(!!completeLog, `Completion: ${completeLog?.slice(0, 60) || 'NOT FOUND'}`)

    // ═══════ T7: GET /status ═══════
    log.step('T7: GET /status/:taskId')
    await page.waitForTimeout(500)
    const st = await withTimeout(httpReq('GET', `http://127.0.0.1:${mcpPort}/status/${taskId}`), 5000, 'GET /status')
    assert(st?.status === 200, 'HTTP 200')
    assert(st?.body?.status === 'completed', `status=${st?.body?.status}`)
    if (st?.body?.result) {
      assert(st.body.result.includes('MCP_TEST_OK'), 'MCP_TEST_OK in result')
      log.info(`Result: ${st.body.result.substring(0, 80)}...`)
    }

    // ═══════ T8: Delivery logs ═══════
    log.step('T8: Delivery')
    const dLogs = findInLogs(mainProcessLogs, '[MCP:deliver]')
    assert(dLogs.length > 0, `Delivery entries: ${dLogs.length}`)

    // ═══════ SUMMARY ═══════
    clearInterval(logPump)
    console.log('\n' + '═'.repeat(45))
    console.log(`  Passed: ${passed}  Failed: ${failed}`)
    if (failed > 0) { process.exitCode = 1; log.fail('SOME TESTS FAILED') }
    else log.pass('ALL TESTS PASSED')
    console.log('═'.repeat(45))

    // Dump filtered main logs
    console.log('\n--- MCP/Claude Logs (last 50) ---')
    mainProcessLogs
      .filter(l => MCP_FILTER.test(l))
      .slice(-50)
      .forEach(l => console.log(l.replace(/^\[(stdout|stderr)\]\s*/, '').trim().slice(0, 160)))

  } finally {
    clearTimeout(globalTimer)
    if (app) {
      log.info('Closing app...')
      await app.close().catch(() => {})
    }
  }
}

main().catch(err => {
  console.error(`\n${c.F}[FATAL]${c.R}`, err.message)
  console.error(err.stack)
  process.exit(1)
})

```

<thinking>
Now I can see the root cause clearly:

```
[MCP:Delegate] Claude sub-agent tab created: new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg-tab-12
[MCP:Delegate] Error: Claude terminal not found after creation
```

The key error: **"Claude terminal not found after creation"**. 

The terminal IPC from the renderer creates the tab with tabId `new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg-tab-12`, but when the main process tries `terminals.get(claudeTabId)`, it returns `undefined`.

Why? Because the `terminal:create` IPC handler stores the PTY in `terminals` using the tabId that was sent by the renderer. 

There's likely a race condition where the renderer initiates the tab creation and PTY setup, but the delegation code queries for the terminal before the main process has finished storing it in the `terminals` map. Setting up the IPC communication between renderer and main process...

The real issue might be the invalid CWD for the PTY: `cwd=__unset__new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg`. Even though the PTY is created successfully (I can see it in the logs with pid=21163), the shell might fail to initialize properly with that malformed working directory, or the PTY isn't being stored correctly in the terminals map.

Looking at how the tabId is generated in App.tsx, the store creates it as `${projectId}-tab-${Date.now() % 10000}`, and this same tabId should be used consistently across the IPC calls. But if `claudeTabId` is different from what was actually stored in the terminals map, that would explain why the lookup fails. WAIT — I think I see it! There might be a mismatch between what `createTab` returns and what `terminal:create` stores. Let me trace through the code flow:

In `createTab`, it generates a `tabId` and sends it to the main process via `terminal:create`, which stores the PTY process under that same `tabId` and returns the process ID. The renderer then uses that `tabId` when notifying about the tab creation.

Unless there's a timing issue where the MCP handler fires before `terminal:create` finishes, but that shouldn't happen since `createTab` awaits the invoke call. Let me look at what happens in the App.tsx handler when it receives the MCP message...

Examining the handler logic... I'm tracing through the async flow to verify the ordering is correct, but I'm noticing a discrepancy—the PTY:CREATED log shows one tabId format, yet the error at line 805 is looking for a different `claudeTabId` that doesn't exist in the terminals map, which suggests the tabId being used to look up the terminal might be wrong or getting lost somewhere in the handoff between renderer and main. Let me look at the log order:
1. `[MCP:Delegate] Claude sub-agent tab created: new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg-tab-12`
2. But `terminals.get('new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg-tab-12')` returns undefined?

This is strange. The PTY:CREATED log clearly shows the terminal was created. Unless there's a race condition where `terminal:create` hasn't completed yet when `mcp:sub-agent-tab-created` fires.

Wait, actually: `ipcRenderer.invoke` is async. The renderer awaits the result, so that should ensure the main process handler completes first. But let me trace through the `createTab` implementation more carefully—maybe the tabId being generated on the renderer side doesn't match what the main process stores, or perhaps the `terminal:create` call is failing silently before the PTY gets added to the map. I'm wondering if the `claudeTabId` being used in `delegateToClaudeSubAgent` is actually different from the `tabId` that gets stored in the terminals map—the renderer generates the tab ID with a specific format, sends it to main for storage, then sends it again via the sub-agent message, but something might be getting lost or transformed in that handoff. The `delegateToClaudeSubAgent` should resolve with that tabId, and then `terminals.get('...-tab-12')` should find the PTY. But what if the `terminals` Map gets cleaned up by another handler, like when a terminal is killed? Or maybe the ghost tabs from previous runs are being restored and automatically killing themselves if they have `wasInterrupted: true`. I'm wondering if the `__unset__` CWD prefix is causing the PTY to fail and exit immediately, which would trigger the `ptyProcess.onExit` handler and remove it from the map.

Checking the exit handler...

it deletes the terminal from `terminals` when the process exits. So if the shell exits right away because of an invalid CWD, the terminal gets removed before the delegation code can access it. That would explain the ghost tabs, but tab-12 is the new one—unless it's also exiting immediately? The CWD `__unset__new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg` isn't a valid path, so spawning the shell with that directory will likely fail or just start in whatever the current working directory is.

On macOS, if the CWD doesn't exist, the shell might fall back to $HOME, start but immediately exit, or throw an error. If it starts but exits right away—like if the shell tries to cd to that invalid path during initialization—the `onExit` handler fires and removes the terminal before the delegation message gets processed. That's the race condition: the renderer gets back the pid from `terminal:create`, but by the time the `mcp:sub-agent-tab-created` message arrives, the terminal's already been deleted from `terminals`.

The real issue is that `ppid=0` causes `findTabByChildPid` to fail, so it falls back to grabbing the first terminal from the Map, which happens to be from the `runtime-tests` project. The main process then sends `mcp:create-sub-agent-tab` to the renderer with that wrong geminiTabId, and the renderer tries to create a sub-agent tab using a CWD that doesn't exist.

When the renderer receives the request, it looks up the geminiTabId in the active project's tabs, but since that ID belongs to a different project, it's not found. The fallback tries to use the active project's path, but that's also problematic—the tab's CWD is set to something like `__unset__new_project_1770875324588_cvf`, which is clearly invalid.

Looking at how tabs are created, the store should be setting the CWD to either the passed value, the workspace path, or the process CWD, but something's going wrong in that chain. The issue seems to be that either the workspace isn't being found when the tab was created, or the CWD wasn't properly initialized in the first place. and exists in `openProjects`, then `workspace` is defined. And `workspace.projectPath` should be the project path.

Looking at the tab data, all the Claude sub-agent tabs have `cwd: "__unset__new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg"` — tabs 9, 10, and 11 are leftover from previous runs, while tab 12 is the new one. That `__unset__` prefix looks like a placeholder, which makes me think the issue might be in `openProject` when a new project is created with a base64-encoded `projectPath` but hasn't been saved to the database yet, causing `getProjectById` to return `null`.

The logs confirm this — when looking up the `runtime-tests` project by its base64-encoded ID, the database returns nothing, and then `saveTabs` skips saving because it can't find the project.

Meanwhile, the `new_project_1770875324588_cvfvsg` project does exist in the database, but the tabs saved under it have a malformed CWD of `__unset__new_project_...`, which suggests the CWD was never properly initialized when those tabs were created in an earlier test run.

The core issue is that when a sub-agent tab is created, it's getting an invalid CWD because the geminiTabId doesn't match any actual tab in the active project's workspace — I need to fix the lookup logic in the App.tsx handler to properly resolve the tab reference.

There are three interconnected bugs here: the CWD mismatch causing the sub-agent tab to fail, the terminal exiting immediately due to the bad CWD before the delegation can complete, and ghost tabs persisting in the database from previous test runs. The most direct fix is to pass the CWD from the main process directly in the IPC message rather than trying to look it up in the renderer.

Fixing the CWD lookup... Adding retry logic with delays...

```diff
-   const claudeTabId = await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => reject(new Error('Sub-agent tab creation timeout')), 10000);
    // IPC invoke to renderer → creates tab → returns tabId
    mainWindow.webContents.send('mcp:create-sub-agent-tab', {
      taskId,
      geminiTabId,
    });
    // Renderer will reply via IPC
    ipcMain.once('mcp:sub-agent-tab-created', (event, data) => {
      clearTimeout(timeout);
      if (data.error) reject(new Error(data.error));
      else resolve(data.tabId);
    });
  });

  task.claudeTabId = claudeTabId;
  task.status = 'starting';
  subAgentParentTab.set(claudeTabId, geminiTabId);

  console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Claude sub-agent tab created: ' + claudeTabId);

  // 3. Launch Claude in the sub-agent tab
  const claudeTerm = terminals.get(claudeTabId);
  if (!claudeTerm) {
    throw new Error('Claude terminal not found after creation');
  }
+   // Resolve CWD from main process (renderer may not find cross-project tabs)
  const geminiCwd = terminalProjects.get(geminiTabId) || process.cwd();
  console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Using CWD from main: ' + geminiCwd);

  const claudeTabId = await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => reject(new Error('Sub-agent tab creation timeout')), 10000);
    // IPC invoke to renderer → creates tab → returns tabId
    mainWindow.webContents.send('mcp:create-sub-agent-tab', {
      taskId,
      geminiTabId,
      cwd: geminiCwd,
    });
    // Renderer will reply via IPC
    ipcMain.once('mcp:sub-agent-tab-created', (event, data) => {
      clearTimeout(timeout);
      if (data.error) reject(new Error(data.error));
      else resolve(data.tabId);
    });
  });

  task.claudeTabId = claudeTabId;
  task.status = 'starting';
  subAgentParentTab.set(claudeTabId, geminiTabId);

  console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Claude sub-agent tab created: ' + claudeTabId);

  // 3. Launch Claude in the sub-agent tab
  // Retry with delay: PTY might not be in terminals yet if shell exits/restarts quickly
  let claudeTerm = null;
  for (let retry = 0; retry < 5; retry++) {
    claudeTerm = terminals.get(claudeTabId);
    if (claudeTerm) break;
    console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Terminal not found yet, retry ' + (retry + 1) + '/5...');
    await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, 500));
  }
  if (!claudeTerm) {
    throw new Error('Claude terminal not found after creation (tabId=' + claudeTabId + ', terminals.size=' + terminals.size + ')');
  }
```

```diff
-     const handleMcpCreateSubAgent = async (_: any, data: { taskId: string; geminiTabId: string }) => {
      const state = useWorkspaceStore.getState();
      const { activeProjectId, openProjects } = state;
      if (!activeProjectId) {
        ipcRenderer.send('mcp:sub-agent-tab-created', { error: 'No active project' });
        return;
      }

      // Find the Gemini tab's cwd for the sub-agent
      const workspace = openProjects.get(activeProjectId);
      const geminiTab = workspace?.tabs.get(data.geminiTabId);
      const cwd = geminiTab?.cwd || workspace?.projectPath || '';
+     const handleMcpCreateSubAgent = async (_: any, data: { taskId: string; geminiTabId: string; cwd?: string }) => {
      const state = useWorkspaceStore.getState();
      const { activeProjectId, openProjects } = state;
      if (!activeProjectId) {
        ipcRenderer.send('mcp:sub-agent-tab-created', { error: 'No active project' });
        return;
      }

      // Use CWD from main process (reliable), fallback to Gemini tab or project path
      const workspace = openProjects.get(activeProjectId);
      const geminiTab = workspace?.tabs.get(data.geminiTabId);
      const cwd = data.cwd || geminiTab?.cwd || workspace?.projectPath || '';
```

## Claude
<thinking>
Now I can see the full flow! The CWD fix worked (real path now). The flow progressed much further:

1. ✅ Claude launched successfully in sub-agent tab
2. ✅ Handshake detected: `[Claude Handshake] Tab ... Prompt detected. Starting debounce...`
3. ✅ Bridge detected session: `session=1e009a22...`
4. ❌ BUT: **Completion fired too early!** The MCP completion detector saw `⏵` prompt and triggered BEFORE the handshake even sent the prompt!

The problem:


The detector fires on Claude's initial startup prompt before any actual task is sent, which causes it to try reading a JSONL file that doesn't exist yet. The handshake's 300ms debounce is meant to give Claude time to receive the real prompt, but the completion handler already marks the task done. I need to gate the detector so it only activates after the handshake has actually delivered the prompt to Claude. Looking at the sequence more carefully, the issue is that `task.status` gets set to 'running' before the handshake actually completes, so the MCP completion detector fires prematurely and reads an empty session file. The real fix is to skip the MCP completion detector when the tab is still in a handshake state — I should check if `claudeState` is set to `WAITING_PROMPT` or `DEBOUNCE_PROMPT` and bail out early, or only trigger completion when the handshake is fully done. I see the issue now—during the handshake, `claudeState` is present for that tab, so I can use that as a signal to skip the MCP completion check. Once the handshake finishes and the prompt is sent, `claudeState` gets deleted, so the detector will work normally. Let me verify this approach by checking the MCP completion detector logic...

Updating the detector... I need to add a check for `!claudeState.has(tabId)` to prevent triggering completion while the handshake is still in progress. The real issue is timing: the MCP detector needs to wait until Claude has actually responded to the user's prompt, not just shown the initial thinking indicator. The handshake clears `claudeState` after sending the prompt, so the next thinking indicator should correctly trigger completion—but the 500ms debounce might catch the same indicator that initiated the handshake. Looking at the code flow more carefully, the state gets set to 'DEBOUNCE_PROMPT' at the initial detection, then the setTimeout callback at 300ms runs safePasteAndSubmit and only deletes the state after that completes. So when the MCP detector fires at 500ms, the state should still exist if the async operation is still in flight. I could track completion explicitly with a flag like `mcpHandshakeComplete`, but actually the cleanest solution is to use the task status itself—keep it as 'handshake' until the handshake callback completes, then set it to 'running', since the MCP detector already checks for that status. The issue is the handshake callback lives in the onData handler, not in the delegateToClaudeSubAgent function, so I need a way to signal when it's done. The safest fix is just adding a `!claudeState.has(tabId)` check to the MCP completion detector to prevent it from firing while Claude is still processing.

I should also add a guard to ignore the first prompt detection—maybe a minimum wait time or just skip if the handshake is still in progress. Looking at the logs though, there's something else going wrong: the task is completing but the session file lookup is failing, which suggests the response handling is breaking down somewhere.

Actually, I see the real issue now. The initial trigger fires both the handshake and the completion detector at different debounce intervals—handshake at 300ms, completion at 500ms. By the time completion fires, the handshake callback is still running and `claudeState` is still set, so the guard wouldn't catch it anyway. The state transitions from WAITING_PROMPT to DEBOUNCE_PROMPT, then more data arrives and things get tangled up.

But there's a bigger problem: the completion detector pattern is checking for `>` which is way too broad since shell output contains that character everywhere. It should be checking for the actual completion indicator like `❯` instead. That's causing the detector to fire on basically any output.

The fix is twofold—make the pattern more specific and skip completion detection entirely during the handshake phase. detector: add `!claudeState.has(tabId)` guard. Also change the `>` to `❯` (U+276F) to avoid false positives from regular shell output. The handshake detector already has the `claudeState` guard which prevents it from firing unless we're explicitly waiting for a prompt, but the MCP detector is missing this protection.

Looking at the test output, I can see the sequence: the ⏵ prompt gets detected by both detectors, then 500ms later the MCP detector fires and triggers `handleSubAgentCompletion`.
</thinking>

## Claude
Отлично, прогресс! CWD фикс работает. Теперь вижу новую проблему — **race condition**: MCP completion detector сработал НА ПЕРВОМ `⏵` (когда Claude только запустился), ДО того как handshake отправил промпт. Результат: "No JSONL response found".

Последовательность:
1. Claude запущен → показывает `⏵` → **оба** детектора видят его
2. Handshake (300ms debounce) → отправляет промпт
3. MCP Detector (500ms debounce) → `handleSubAgentCompletion` → нет JSONL → "no response"

Фикс: MCP detector должен пропускать, если handshake ещё активен (`claudeState.has(tabId)`).

## Claude
The `readLatestAssistantMessage` uses `findSessionFile(sessionId, cwd)`. The session JSONL is at `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/<sessionId>.jsonl`, where the slug is derived from the CWD. If `cwd` is `/Users/fedor/Desktop/custom-terminal/runtime-tests`, the slug won't match the actual project directory.

But this is an issue with the test setup (ppid=0 fallback), not the production flow. For production, the Gemini PID will correctly resolve, and the CWD will be correct.

## Claude
<thinking>
Good progress! Looking at the logs:

1. Handshake fires and sends the prompt ✅
2. After handshake sends prompt and clears, the MCP detector fires
3. But it STILL reads JSONL too early!

The issue is clearer now. The sequence:
1. Claude starts → ⏵ (initial prompt) 
2. Handshake catches it (WAITING_PROMPT) → sets DEBOUNCE_PROMPT → 300ms debounce
3. MCP detector SKIPPED (because claudeState.has(tabId) = true) ✅ 


4. Handshake debounce fires → sends prompt via safePasteAndSubmit → claudeState.delete(tabId)
5. Claude receives prompt → starts processing → re-renders (shows the prompt text)
6. During Claude's processing, the TUI shows various output... at some point ⏵ or ❯ appears
7. MCP detector sees it → 500ms debounce → fires handleSubAgentCompletion

But looking at the actual log, the handshake is firing and sending the prompt, though the log output seems to be getting cut off mid-message. The handshake resets when more data arrives during the debounce window, and after the prompt is sent at +446ms, additional data from Claude's processing triggers another reset—but since `claudePendingPrompt` is already cleared, it correctly reports no pending prompt. The real issue is that the MCP detector fires immediately after the prompt is sent, before Claude has even finished rendering its response, so it's catching the processing indicator or cursor character instead of waiting for actual output.

I need to add a cooldown mechanism using a Map that tracks when prompts were sent per tab, then have the MCP detector skip detection for at least 5 seconds after a prompt completes. Looking at the logs more carefully, the detector might also be too sensitive to the character matching—Claude uses ⏵ (U+23F5) rather than ❯, so I should verify which character is actually triggering the false positive. changed the detector to check for `\u23F5` and `\u276F`. Let me think about what Claude shows...

Claude's prompt is `⏵` (U+23F5). After the user sends a message, Claude shows processing and then the response, followed by another `⏵` prompt.

But when the handshake sends the prompt text via safePasteAndSubmit, the PTY shows the pasted text and then Enter. Claude then processes it. During processing, it might show `⏵` or `❯` in the interface (e.g., in the prompt line above the response area).

The issue is that Claude's TUI re-renders and the detector catches intermediate renders.

Looking at the test timing, the handshake sends Enter around 446ms after starting, then the UI settles and fires the debounce reset. When the detector runs and finds no pending prompt, it tries to send again but the prompt's already been consumed. At that point, `claudeState` was already deleted by the first handshake callback after safePasteAndSubmit completed. So when more data arrives from Claude processing the input and rendering the response, the `claudeState.has(tabId)` check fails and the MCP detector doesn't fire. I'm tracing through the async flow more carefully — when the handshake callback fires and sends the prompt via safePasteAndSubmit, additional data arrives from the PTY during that operation, which resets the debounce timer in the onData handler. Then when safePasteAndSubmit completes and deletes claudeState, a new debounce timer that was just set fires again, triggering the "No pending prompt found" message because the prompt was already consumed. The real problem underneath all this timing complexity is that the MCP completion detector is firing too early, right after the prompt gets sent but before Claude has actually started responding.

The solution is to add a time guard — I'll track when the prompt was sent and prevent the MCP detector from firing for at least 5 seconds after that. I'm creating a Map to store the timestamp for each tab, then checking that elapsed time in the detector's debounce callback before allowing it to proceed.

Adding timestamp tracking...
</thinking>

Fix: add a minimum cooldown — don't fire completion within 5s of the prompt being sent.

## Claude

**Actions:**

```diff
-             // Double-check handshake still not active (could have been set during debounce)
            if (claudeState.has(tabId) || claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {

+             // Double-check handshake still not active (could have been set during debounce)
            if (claudeState.has(tabId) || claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — handshake still active for: ' + tabId);
              return;
            }
            // Cooldown: don't fire within 5s of prompt being sent (Claude needs time to process)
            var sentAt = subAgentPromptSentAt.get(tabId);
            if (sentAt && Date.now() - sentAt < 5000) {
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — cooldown (' + (Date.now() - sentAt) + 'ms since prompt sent)');
              return;

## Claude
<thinking>
The cooldown is working — I can see:```
[MCP:Detector] Skipping — cooldown (521ms since prompt sent)[MCP:Detector] Skipping — cooldown (2756ms since prompt sent)
```The MCP detector skipped two detections correctly. But then it never fired again within the test window.

Looking at the test output:
```
[36m[06:43:26][STEP][0m T5: Claude handshake (watch for PTY output)...
[32m[06:43:34][PASS][0m Handshake: ...


[32m[06:43:37][PASS][0m SessionID: 36213381...
[36m[06:43:37][STEP][0m T6: Completion (wait for [MCPResult])
[2m[06:43:47][INFO][0m Waiting... 10s
...60s
[31m[06:44:32][FAIL][0m [MCPResult]: TIMEOUT 65000ms
```

The handshake and session ID both passed, the cooldown correctly suppressed the initial detections, but the detector never triggered again after that — the test timed out waiting for the MCPResult.

The issue is likely that Claude finished the simple prompt in under 5 seconds and showed the completion indicator, but the cooldown period was still active, so the detector skipped it. Once the cooldown ended, there was no new indicator to catch because Claude was already waiting at the prompt. I need to either shorten the cooldown window or queue detections that occur during cooldown and fire them once the window closes.

The most reliable approach is to check the actual JSONL response file instead of relying on timing — if there's a new assistant message in the session, it's a genuine completion worth handling.

Checking the response file... Setting up a deferred re-check approach instead — if we detect the ⏵ symbol during the cooldown period, I'll schedule a timer to check the JSONL again once the cooldown expires, rather than skipping the detection entirely.

Wait, but the detector itself has debouncing, so repeated ⏵ symbols reset the timer. The actual problem is that after cooldown ends, there's no new ⏵ to trigger another check since Claude's already idle.

Let me reconsider this. The cleanest solution is to check the JSONL file directly once the cooldown expires, rather than waiting for another ⏵ detection. If a response exists, complete the task. Otherwise, set up the watcher to catch the next ⏵ that appears after the cooldown period.

The issue with that approach is it requires polling the JSONL, which contradicts the event-driven design. Let me try a state-based counter instead: mark the tab as "waiting" after sending the prompt, have the detector skip detections during that phase, then allow the first detection after that phase to trigger completion.

Actually, the simplest fix is to defer the check itself—when the detector fires during cooldown, schedule it to run again once the cooldown expires, and at that point check if the JSONL has content to complete.
</thinking>

## Claude
Cooldown works but Claude responds in <5s — the completion ⏵ gets skipped. Need to defer instead of skip. When ⏵ seen during cooldown, schedule a check for when cooldown expires.

```diff
-           clearTimeout(subAgentCompletionTimers.get(tabId));
          subAgentCompletionTimers.set(tabId, setTimeout(() => {
            subAgentCompletionTimers.delete(tabId);
            // Double-check handshake still not active (could have been set during debounce)
            if (claudeState.has(tabId) || claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — handshake still active for: ' + tabId);
              return;
            }
            // Cooldown: don't fire within 5s of prompt being sent (Claude needs time to process)
            var sentAt = subAgentPromptSentAt.get(tabId);
            if (sentAt && Date.now() - sentAt < 5000) {
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — cooldown (' + (Date.now() - sentAt) + 'ms since prompt sent)');
              return;
            }
            console.log('[MCP:Detector] Prompt detected in sub-agent tab: ' + tabId);
            // Only trigger if there's a running task for this tab
            let hasRunningTask = false;
            for (const [, t] of mcpTasks) {
              if (t.claudeTabId === tabId && t.status === 'running') { hasRunningTask = true; break; }
            }
            if (hasRunningTask) {
              handleSubAgentCompletion(tabId);
            }
          }, 500));
+           clearTimeout(subAgentCompletionTimers.get(tabId));
          // Calculate debounce delay: normal 500ms, or defer to cooldown end if within cooldown
          var debounceMs = 500;
          var sentAt = subAgentPromptSentAt.get(tabId);
          if (sentAt) {
            var elapsed = Date.now() - sentAt;
            if (elapsed < 5000) {
              // Defer: schedule check for when cooldown expires + 1s buffer
              debounceMs = (5000 - elapsed) + 1000;
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Deferring check by ' + debounceMs + 'ms (cooldown, ' + elapsed + 'ms since prompt)');
            }
          }
          subAgentCompletionTimers.set(tabId, setTimeout(() => {
            subAgentCompletionTimers.delete(tabId);
            // Double-check handshake still not active
            if (claudeState.has(tabId) || claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {
              console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — handshake still active for: ' + tabId);
              return;
            }
            console.log('[MCP:Detector] Prompt detected in sub-agent tab: ' + tabId);
            // Only trigger if there's a running task for this tab
            let hasRunningTask = false;
            for (const [, t] of mcpTasks) {
              if (t.claudeTabId === tabId && t.status === 'running') { hasRunningTask = true; break; }
            }
            if (hasRunningTask) {
              handleSubAgentCompletion(tabId);
            }
          }, debounceMs));

2. Multiple deferred detections during cooldown (3-6s)

## Claude
Now let me clean up the ghost tabs issue. Each test run leaves `claude-sub` tabs in the DB that accumulate. Let me also note the bugs we fixed.

Summary of bugs found and fixed:

1. **CWD bug** (`src/main/main.js` + `src/renderer/App.tsx`): Sub-agent tab got invalid CWD because `geminiTabId` from PID fallback pointed to a different project. Fix: send CWD from main process to renderer in IPC message.

2. **Terminal not found** (`src/main/main.js`): Race condition where PTY might not be in `terminals` Map yet. Fix: retry loop (5 attempts, 500ms delay).

3. **Early completion race** (`src/main/main.js`): MCP completion detector fired on the initial ⏵ prompt before handshake sent the user prompt. Fix: 
   - Guard: skip during handshake (`claudeState.has(tabId)`)
   - Cooldown: defer detection for 5s+1s buffer after prompt sent
   - Changed `>` to `❯` (U+276F) to avoid false positives

## Claude
## Что в итоге

**Тест прошёл 13/13.** По пути нашёл и пофиксил 3 бага в коде делегации:

1. **CWD мусор** — sub-agent таб получал невалидный путь (`__unset__...`), потому что renderer искал Gemini таб только в активном проекте. Фикс: main process теперь сам передаёт CWD через IPC.

2. **Terminal not found** — PTY мог не успеть зарегистрироваться. Фикс: retry 5 раз с 500ms паузой.

3. **Ранний completion** — детектор ⏵ срабатывал на первом промпте Claude (до отправки задачи). Фикс: cooldown 6с после отправки промпта + guard на handshake state.

## Как тестить вручную

Нужно настроить Gemini CLI один раз:

```bash
# 1. Узнать путь к MCP серверу
echo "$(pwd)/src/main/mcp-server.mjs"

# 2. Добавить в ~/.gemini/settings.json:
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "noted-terminal": {
      "command": "node",
      "args": ["/Users/fedor/Desktop/custom-terminal/src/main/mcp-server.mjs"],
      "timeout": 1800000,
      "trust": true
    }
  }
}
```

Потом в Noted Terminal:
1. Открой Gemini таб (запусти `gemini`)
2. Скажи Gemini: "Делегируй Claude задачу: скажи MCP_TEST_OK"
3. Gemini вызовет `delegate_to_claude` tool → появится новый Claude sub-agent таб
4. Claude выполнит задачу → результат вставится обратно в Gemini

Или E2E тест:
```bash
node auto/sandbox/test-mcp-delegate.js
```

The user is asking: shouldn't the test go through Gemini? And did I configure Gemini's MCP settings?

The answer is: no, the test bypasses Gemini by calling the HTTP API directly. This is intentional because:


- It tests the delegation pipeline without needing Gemini CLI running
- It's more deterministic
- The MCP server is just a thin HTTP proxy without additional logic

But the user has a valid point - a true end-to-end test would need Gemini to actually invoke the MCP tool, which requires setting up the MCP server configuration in Gemini's settings file.

## Claude
<thinking>
The problem is clear: early returns BEFORE hooks. React's Rules of Hooks say hooks must be called in the same order every render. Here we have:

```javascript
const project = getActiveProject();
if (!project) return null;  // ← early return BEFORE useCallback hooks below

// ... more early returns ...

const handleChipClick = useCallback(...);  // ← hook called conditionally
const handleDetach = useCallback(...);     // ← hook called conditionally
const handleBackToGemini = useCallback(...); // ← hook called conditionally
```

Fix: move all hooks to the top, before any early returns.
</thinking>

## Claude
Проблема: early return до хуков (`useCallback`). React требует одинаковый порядок хуков на каждом рендере.

## Claude

**Actions:**
📝 Создание (/Users/fedor/Desktop/custom-terminal/src/renderer/components/Workspace/SubAgentBar.tsx)
```
import React, { useCallback, useMemo } from 'react';
import { useWorkspaceStore } from '../../store/useWorkspaceStore';

interface SubAgentBarProps {
  projectId: string;
  viewingSubAgentTabId: string | null;
  onViewSubAgent: (tabId: string | null) => void;
}

export default function SubAgentBar({ projectId, viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent }: SubAgentBarProps) {
  const getActiveProject = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getActiveProject);
  const getSubAgentTabs = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getSubAgentTabs);

  const project = getActiveProject();
  const activeTabId = project?.activeTabId;
  const activeTab = activeTabId ? project?.tabs.get(activeTabId) : null;

  const subAgentTabs = useMemo(() => {
    if (!activeTabId || activeTab?.commandType !== 'gemini') return [];
    return getSubAgentTabs(activeTabId);
  }, [activeTabId, activeTab?.commandType, getSubAgentTabs]);

  const handleChipClick = useCallback((tabId: string) => {
    if (viewingSubAgentTabId === tabId) {
      onViewSubAgent(null);
    } else {
      onViewSubAgent(tabId);
    }
  }, [viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleDetach = useCallback((e: React.MouseEvent, tabId: string) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    e.stopPropagation();
    const state = useWorkspaceStore.getState();
    state.setTabParent(tabId, '');
    onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleBackToGemini = useCallback(() => {
    onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [onViewSubAgent]);

  // Early return AFTER all hooks
  if (!project || !activeTabId || !activeTab) return null;
  if (activeTab.commandType !== 'gemini') return null;
  if (subAgentTabs.length === 0) return null;

  return (
    <div
      className="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-2 border-b border-border-main"
      style={{
        height: '28px',
        backgroundColor: 'rgba(30, 30, 30, 0.95)',
        fontSize: '11px',
      }}
    >
      {viewingSubAgentTabId && (
        <button
          onClick={handleBackToGemini}
          className="flex items-center gap-1 px-1.5 py-0.5 rounded text-[10px] hover:bg-white/10 transition-colors"
          style={{ color: 'rgba(255,255,255,0.5)' }}
        >
          ← Gemini
        </button>
      )}

      <span style={{ color: 'rgba(255,255,255,0.35)', fontSize: '10px' }}>Sub-agents:</span>

      {subAgentTabs.map((tab, i) => {
        const isViewing = viewingSubAgentTabId === tab.id;
        const isRunning = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'running' || (!tab.claudeAgentStatus && tab.claudeSessionId);
        const isDone = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'done';
        const isError = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'error';

        let statusIcon = '⟳';
        let statusColor = 'rgba(255,255,255,0.6)';
        if (isDone) { statusIcon = '✓'; statusColor = '#a6e3a1'; }
        if (isError) { statusIcon = '✗'; statusColor = '#f38ba8'; }

        return (
          <button
            key={tab.id}
            onClick={() => handleChipClick(tab.id)}
            onContextMenu={(e) => handleDetach(e, tab.id)}
            className="flex items-center gap-1 px-2 py-0.5 rounded transition-colors"
            style={{
              backgroundColor: isViewing ? 'rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.3)' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.06)',
              border: isViewing ? '1px solid rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.5)' : '1px solid transparent',
              color: isViewing ? '#cc7832' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.7)',
              cursor: 'pointer',
            }}
            title="Click to view, right-click to detach"
          >
            <span style={{ fontSize: '10px' }}>🤖</span>
            <span>Claude #{i + 1}</span>
            <span style={{ color: statusColor, fontSize: '10px' }}>{statusIcon}</span>
          </button>
        );
      })}
    </div>
  );
}

```

## User
This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Analysis:
Let me chronologically analyze the conversation:

1. **Context from previous session**: The user had already implemented a complete "Gemini → Claude MCP Delegation System" in a previous conversation. The plan had 6 pieces (Backend + Frontend). All 6 steps were implemented and validated. The current session continues from that work.

2. **User's first message (implicit from context)**: The task was to write E2E tests for the MCP delegation system, specifically `test-mcp-delegate.js` and `test-sub-agent-bar.js`. The user wanted tests written in `auto/sandbox/`.

3. **My approach**: I read the test infrastructure (`auto/context.md`, `auto/core/launcher.js`, existing tests), then read the MCP implementation in `main.js` to understand the flow, then wrote and ran the test.

4. **First test run**: The test hung with no visible output. The user got frustrated ("я заебал почему сейчас терминал просто на этом тесте но тупо завис") - they wanted real-time progress output and a 20-second timeout for failures.

5. **Second test version**: Added `logMainProcess: true` but this flooded stdout with huge project data dumps (35627 chars truncated), making test progress invisible. Hit 180s global timeout.

6. **Third test version**: Set `logMainProcess: false` (capture silently, don't print), added filtered MCP log streaming, shorter timeouts, `withTimeout()` wrapper. Now could see progress. T1-T4 passed but T5 failed with: `[MCP:Delegate] Error: Claude terminal not found after creation` and CWD was `__unset__new_project_...`.

7. **Bug #1 - CWD**: The `geminiTabId` from PID fallback (ppid=0) pointed to a tab in a different project. Renderer couldn't find it → CWD fell back to garbage. Fix: main process sends CWD to renderer via IPC. Also fixed App.tsx to prefer `data.cwd`.

8. **Bug #2 - Terminal not found**: Added retry loop (5 attempts, 500ms) in `delegateToClaudeSubAgent` for `terminals.get()`.

9. **Fourth test run**: CWD fixed, Claude launched, handshake worked, BUT `[MCP:Detector]` fired on the FIRST ⏵ prompt (before handshake sent the user prompt). `readLatestAssistantMessage` found no JSONL → delivered empty result.

10. **Bug #3 - Race condition**: Added guard: skip MCP detector when `claudeState.has(tabId)` or `claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)`. Changed `>` to `❯` (U+276F) in detector.

11. **Fifth test run**: Guard worked for initial prompt, but Claude responded in <5s. The cooldown skipped the completion ⏵: `[MCP:Detector] Skipping — cooldown (521ms since prompt sent)` and `(2756ms since prompt sent)`. Then no more ⏵ detected.

12. **Fix**: Changed from "skip during cooldown" to "defer during cooldown" — schedule check for when cooldown expires. Added `subAgentPromptSentAt` Map and deferred timer calculation.

13. **Sixth test run**: 13/13 PASSED. Full pipeline works.

14. **User reports ErrorBoundary in SubAgentBar.tsx**: "Rendered more hooks than during the previous render" — classic hooks ordering violation. Early returns before `useCallback` hooks.

15. **Fix SubAgentBar.tsx**: Moved all hooks (`useMemo`, `useCallback`) before any early returns. Rewrote component to compute data first, call all hooks, then do conditional returns.

16. **Final test run**: 13/13 PASSED after hooks fix.

17. **User asked about manual testing**: I explained the test bypasses Gemini (direct HTTP), and for full pipeline they need Gemini MCP config.

18. **User asked me to configure Gemini**: Added `noted-terminal` MCP server to `~/.gemini/settings.json`.

19. **User reported SubAgentBar ErrorBoundary**: I fixed the hooks ordering issue and ran the test again - 13/13 passed.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user wanted E2E tests written for the MCP delegation system (Gemini → Claude sub-agent) that was implemented in a previous session. Specifically:
   - Write and run `auto/sandbox/test-mcp-delegate.js` — full pipeline E2E test
   - Write `auto/sandbox/test-sub-agent-bar.js` — UI test for SubAgentBar component
   - If code bugs are found during testing, fix the code (not the test)
   - Configure Gemini CLI's MCP settings for manual testing
   - Fix the SubAgentBar.tsx ErrorBoundary hooks violation
   - After fixing, re-run the E2E test to confirm everything works

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **MCP Delegation Pipeline**: Gemini CLI → mcp-server.mjs → HTTP POST /delegate → Electron main.js → creates Claude sub-agent tab → Claude works → completion detected via ⏵ → JSONL response read → result pasted back into Gemini PTY
   - **Fire-and-forget architecture**: HTTP POST returns taskId immediately, completion is async
   - **PID matching fallback**: `findTabByChildPid(ppid)` with fallback to first terminal when ppid=0
   - **Handshake state machine**: `claudeState` Map tracks WAITING_PROMPT → DEBOUNCE_PROMPT → (prompt sent) → deleted
   - **Completion detection**: PTY onData watches for ⏵ (U+23F5) or ❯ (U+276F) with debounce + cooldown + deferral
   - **safePasteAndSubmit**: Handles macOS TTYHOG 1024-byte limit with bracketed paste chunks
   - **React Rules of Hooks**: All hooks must be called before any early returns
   - **Playwright E2E testing**: `auto/core/launcher.js` for Electron launch, `waitForMainProcessLog` for event-driven assertions

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`src/main/main.js`** — Primary backend, multiple fixes applied:
     - Added `subAgentPromptSentAt` Map (line ~65):
       ```javascript
       const subAgentCompletionTimers = new Map(); // claudeTabId -> debounce timer
       const subAgentPromptSentAt = new Map();     // claudeTabId -> timestamp when prompt was sent
       ```
     - Fixed CWD resolution in `delegateToClaudeSubAgent` (~line 781): sends CWD from main process to renderer:
       ```javascript
       const geminiCwd = terminalProjects.get(geminiTabId) || process.cwd();
       console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Using CWD from main: ' + geminiCwd);
       mainWindow.webContents.send('mcp:create-sub-agent-tab', {
         taskId, geminiTabId, cwd: geminiCwd,
       });
       ```
     - Added terminal retry loop (~line 802):
       ```javascript
       let claudeTerm = null;
       for (let retry = 0; retry < 5; retry++) {
         claudeTerm = terminals.get(claudeTabId);
         if (claudeTerm) break;
         console.log('[MCP:Delegate] Terminal not found yet, retry ' + (retry + 1) + '/5...');
         await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, 500));
       }
       ```
     - Set `subAgentPromptSentAt` timestamp after handshake sends prompt (both STEP 1 and STEP 2 debounce callbacks):
       ```javascript
       if (subAgentParentTab.has(tabId)) subAgentPromptSentAt.set(tabId, Date.now());
       ```
     - Fixed MCP completion detector with handshake guard + deferred cooldown (~line 1387):
       ```javascript
       if (subAgentParentTab.has(tabId) && !claudeState.has(tabId) && !claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {
         const sc = stripVTControlCharacters(data);
         if (sc.includes('\u23F5') || sc.includes('\u276F')) {
           clearTimeout(subAgentCompletionTimers.get(tabId));
           var debounceMs = 500;
           var sentAt = subAgentPromptSentAt.get(tabId);
           if (sentAt) {
             var elapsed = Date.now() - sentAt;
             if (elapsed < 5000) {
               debounceMs = (5000 - elapsed) + 1000;
               console.log('[MCP:Detector] Deferring check by ' + debounceMs + 'ms (cooldown, ' + elapsed + 'ms since prompt)');
             }
           }
           subAgentCompletionTimers.set(tabId, setTimeout(() => {
             subAgentCompletionTimers.delete(tabId);
             if (claudeState.has(tabId) || claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)) {
               console.log('[MCP:Detector] Skipping — handshake still active for: ' + tabId);
               return;
             }
             // ... trigger completion if running task exists
           }, debounceMs));
         }
       }
       ```

   - **`src/renderer/App.tsx`** — Fixed IPC handler to accept CWD from main process (~line 601):

       // ...

     ```

   - **`src/renderer/components/Workspace/SubAgentBar.tsx`** — Complete rewrite to fix hooks ordering. All hooks moved before early returns:
     ```typescript
     export default function SubAgentBar({ projectId, viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent }: SubAgentBarProps) {
       const getActiveProject = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getActiveProject);
       const getSubAgentTabs = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getSubAgentTabs);

       const project = getActiveProject();
       const activeTabId = project?.activeTabId;
       const activeTab = activeTabId ? project?.tabs.get(activeTabId) : null;

       const subAgentTabs = useMemo(() => {
         if (!activeTabId || activeTab?.commandType !== 'gemini') return [];
         return getSubAgentTabs(activeTabId);
       }, [activeTabId, activeTab?.commandType, getSubAgentTabs]);

       const handleChipClick = useCallback((tabId: string) => { /* ... */ }, [viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent]);
       const handleDetach = useCallback((e: React.MouseEvent, tabId: string) => { /* ... */ }, [onViewSubAgent]);
       const handleBackToGemini = useCallback(() => { onViewSubAgent(null); }, [onViewSubAgent]);

       // Early return AFTER all hooks
       if (!project || !activeTabId || !activeTab) return null;
       if (activeTab.commandType !== 'gemini') return null;
       if (subAgentTabs.length === 0) return null;
       // ... render JSX
     ```

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **Test hung with no output (first run)**: `logMainProcess: true` combined with huge project data dumps flooded stdout. User frustrated: "я заебал почему сейчас терминал просто на этом тесте но тупо завис". Fix: set `logMainProcess: false`, added filtered log streaming for MCP-related lines only, added `withTimeout()` wrappers and global timeout.
   
   - **CWD `__unset__new_project_...`**: `geminiTabId` from PID fallback (ppid=0) pointed to a tab from a different project. Renderer couldn't find it in activeProject → CWD fell back to garbage path. Fix: main process resolves CWD from `terminalProjects` Map and sends it via IPC to renderer.
   
   - **`Claude terminal not found after creation`**: PTY with invalid CWD could exit immediately, triggering `terminals.delete()` before delegation code accesses it. Fix: retry loop (5 attempts, 500ms delay).
   
   - **Early completion race condition**: MCP detector fired on the initial ⏵ prompt before handshake sent the user prompt. `readLatestAssistantMessage` found no JSONL. Fix: guard `!claudeState.has(tabId) && !claudePendingPrompt.has(tabId)` + changed `>` to `❯` (U+276F).
   
   - **Cooldown skipping real completion**: 5s cooldown SKIPPED the completion ⏵ when Claude responded in <5s. After cooldown, no new ⏵ appeared. Fix: changed from "skip during cooldown" to "defer during cooldown" — schedule deferred check for `(5000 - elapsed) + 1000` ms.
   
   - **SubAgentBar ErrorBoundary hooks violation**: `[ErrorBoundary] Error: Rendered more hooks than during the previous render.` Early returns (`if (!project) return null`) before `useCallback` hooks violated React Rules of Hooks. Fix: moved all hooks before early returns, used `useMemo` for `subAgentTabs`.

5. Problem Solving:
   - Full MCP delegation pipeline now works end-to-end: 13/13 E2E tests pass
   - Three production bugs found and fixed during testing (CWD, terminal race, completion race)
   - SubAgentBar hooks violation fixed
   - Gemini MCP settings configured for manual testing
   - Ghost `claude-sub` tabs from previous test runs accumulate in DB (noted but not fixed — cosmetic issue)

## Claude
## Текущий UX флоу (глазами пользователя)

### Сценарий: Gemini делегирует задачу Claude

**1. Исходное состояние**
- Открыт таб с Gemini CLI. В TabBar он активен. Пользователь общается с Gemini.

**2. Gemini вызывает MCP tool `delegate_to_claude`**
- Gemini пишет в свой терминал что-то вроде "Using tool: delegate_to_claude..."
- В фоне: main.js создаёт Claude sub-agent таб (`background: true` — таб не появляется в TabBar)
- Claude запускается в скрытом PTY, получает промпт через handshake

**3. SubAgentBar появляется**
- Между TabBar (30px) и терминалом возникает полоска 28px:
  ```
  Sub-agents:  [🤖 Claude #1 ⟳]
  ```
- `⟳` = Claude работает (running)
- TabBar не меняется — Gemini всё ещё "активный" таб

**4. Пользователь кликает на чип "Claude #1"**
- Терминал Gemini скрывается (zIndex: -1)
- Терминал Claude sub-agent показывается (zIndex: 1) — видна реальная работа Claude
- В SubAgentBar появляется кнопка `← Gemini`
- Чип подсвечивается оранжевым (`#cc7832`)
- **TabBar НЕ меняется** — Gemini таб по-прежнему выделен

**5. Пользователь наблюдает за Claude**
- Видит полноценный Claude Code терминал со всем output
- В правом верхнем углу — indigo badge "Claude Agent" с пульсирующей точкой
- Timeline работает, если подключён claudeSessionId

**6. Пользователь кликает `← Gemini` или повторно кликает чип**
- Viewport возвращается к терминалу Gemini

**7. Claude завершает работу**
- Чип меняется: `[🤖 Claude #1 ✓]` (зелёный) или `[🤖 Claude #1 ✗]` (красный при ошибке)
- Результат автоматически вставляется в PTY Gemini через `safePasteAndSubmit`
- Gemini получает ответ и продолжает работу

**8. Правый клик на чип → Detach**
- Sub-agent таб отсоединяется от Gemini (parentTabId = '')
- Становится самостоятельным табом в TabBar
- SubAgentBar скрывается если sub-agent'ов больше нет

---

## Соответствие плану

| Пункт плана | Статус | Комментарий |
|---|---|---|
| **1.1** HTTP Server | ✅ | Работает, порт в `~/.noted-terminal/mcp-port` |
| **1.2** PID Matching | ✅ | `findTabByChildPid` + fallback на ppid=0 |
| **1.3** Task Manager | ✅ | `mcpTasks` Map, `subAgentParentTab` Map |
| **1.4** Completion Detector | ✅ | ⏵/❯ с debounce + cooldown + defer |
| **1.5** Response Reader | ✅ | `readLatestAssistantMessage` из JSONL |
| **1.6** Result Delivery | ✅ | `safePasteAndSubmit` в Gemini PTY через очередь |
| **1.7** MCP Server | ✅ | `mcp-server.mjs`, настроен в `~/.gemini/settings.json` |
| **1.8** Edge cases | ⚠️ Частично | Timeout есть, cleanup при закрытии — не проверен |
| **2.1** Store (parentTabId) | ✅ | `setTabParent`, `getSubAgentTabs` |
| **2.2** SQLite | ✅ | `parent_tab_id` в миграции |
| **2.3** SubAgentBar | ✅ | Работает, hooks fixed |
| **2.4** Workspace integration | ✅ | `viewingSubAgentTabId`, viewport switching |
| **2.5** IPC Listeners | ⚠️ | `mcp:create-sub-agent-tab` ✅, но `mcp:task-status` **не реализован** в renderer |

### Что не реализовано / расхождения с планом:

1. **`mcp:task-status` IPC** — в плане предусмотрен handler в renderer для обновления `claudeAgentStatus`. Сейчас статус обновляется через Terminal.tsx (PTY parsing), но **нет прямого IPC-канала от main → renderer для смены статуса**. Это значит main.js не может напрямую пометить sub-agent как `done`/`error`.

2. **Cleanup при закрытии Gemini** — план говорит: "если Gemini таб закрыт → Ctrl+C в Claude, статус → cancelled". Не проверено, скорее всего не реализовано.

3. **Test `test-sub-agent-bar.js`** — UI тест ещё не написан (pending task).

```diff
- import React, { useCallback, useMemo } from 'react';
import { useWorkspaceStore } from '../../store/useWorkspaceStore';

interface SubAgentBarProps {
  projectId: string;
  viewingSubAgentTabId: string | null;
  onViewSubAgent: (tabId: string | null) => void;
}

export default function SubAgentBar({ projectId, viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent }: SubAgentBarProps) {
  const getActiveProject = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getActiveProject);
  const getSubAgentTabs = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getSubAgentTabs);

  const project = getActiveProject();
  const activeTabId = project?.activeTabId;
  const activeTab = activeTabId ? project?.tabs.get(activeTabId) : null;

  const subAgentTabs = useMemo(() => {
    if (!activeTabId || activeTab?.commandType !== 'gemini') return [];
    return getSubAgentTabs(activeTabId);
  }, [activeTabId, activeTab?.commandType, getSubAgentTabs]);

  const handleChipClick = useCallback((tabId: string) => {
    if (viewingSubAgentTabId === tabId) {
      onViewSubAgent(null);
    } else {
      onViewSubAgent(tabId);
    }
  }, [viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleDetach = useCallback((e: React.MouseEvent, tabId: string) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    e.stopPropagation();
    const state = useWorkspaceStore.getState();
    state.setTabParent(tabId, '');
    onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleBackToGemini = useCallback(() => {
    onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [onViewSubAgent]);

  // Early return AFTER all hooks
  if (!project || !activeTabId || !activeTab) return null;
  if (activeTab.commandType !== 'gemini') return null;
  if (subAgentTabs.length === 0) return null;

  return (
    <div
      className="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-2 border-b border-border-main"
      style={{
        height: '28px',
        backgroundColor: 'rgba(30, 30, 30, 0.95)',
        fontSize: '11px',
      }}
    >
      {viewingSubAgentTabId && (
        <button
          onClick={handleBackToGemini}
          className="flex items-center gap-1 px-1.5 py-0.5 rounded text-[10px] hover:bg-white/10 transition-colors"
          style={{ color: 'rgba(255,255,255,0.5)' }}
        >
          ← Gemini
        </button>
      )}

      <span style={{ color: 'rgba(255,255,255,0.35)', fontSize: '10px' }}>Sub-agents:</span>

      {subAgentTabs.map((tab, i) => {
        const isViewing = viewingSubAgentTabId === tab.id;
        const isRunning = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'running' || (!tab.claudeAgentStatus && tab.claudeSessionId);
        const isDone = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'done';
        const isError = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'error';

        let statusIcon = '⟳';
        let statusColor = 'rgba(255,255,255,0.6)';
        if (isDone) { statusIcon = '✓'; statusColor = '#a6e3a1'; }
        if (isError) { statusIcon = '✗'; statusColor = '#f38ba8'; }

        return (
          <button
            key={tab.id}
            onClick={() => handleChipClick(tab.id)}
            onContextMenu={(e) => handleDetach(e, tab.id)}
            className="flex items-center gap-1 px-2 py-0.5 rounded transition-colors"
            style={{
              backgroundColor: isViewing ? 'rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.3)' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.06)',
              border: isViewing ? '1px solid rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.5)' : '1px solid transparent',
              color: isViewing ? '#cc7832' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.7)',
              cursor: 'pointer',
            }}
            title="Click to view, right-click to detach"
          >
            <span style={{ fontSize: '10px' }}>🤖</span>
            <span>Claude #{i + 1}</span>
            <span style={{ color: statusColor, fontSize: '10px' }}>{statusIcon}</span>
          </button>
        );
      })}
    </div>
  );
}
+ import React, { useCallback, useMemo } from 'react';
import { useWorkspaceStore } from '../../store/useWorkspaceStore';

interface SubAgentBarProps {
  projectId: string;
  viewingSubAgentTabId: string | null;
  onViewSubAgent: (tabId: string | null) => void;
}

export default function SubAgentBar({ projectId, viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent }: SubAgentBarProps) {
  const getActiveProject = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getActiveProject);
  const getSubAgentTabs = useWorkspaceStore((s) => s.getSubAgentTabs);

  const project = getActiveProject();
  const activeTabId = project?.activeTabId;
  const activeTab = activeTabId ? project?.tabs.get(activeTabId) : null;

  const subAgentTabs = useMemo(() => {
    if (!activeTabId || activeTab?.commandType !== 'gemini') return [];
    return getSubAgentTabs(activeTabId);
  }, [activeTabId, activeTab?.commandType, getSubAgentTabs]);

  const handleChipClick = useCallback((tabId: string) => {
    if (viewingSubAgentTabId === tabId) {
      onViewSubAgent(null);
    } else {
      onViewSubAgent(tabId);
    }
  }, [viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleDetach = useCallback((e: React.MouseEvent, tabId: string) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    e.stopPropagation();
    const state = useWorkspaceStore.getState();
    state.setTabParent(tabId, '');
    onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [onViewSubAgent]);

  const handleLabelClick = useCallback(() => {
    if (viewingSubAgentTabId) onViewSubAgent(null);
  }, [viewingSubAgentTabId, onViewSubAgent]);

  // Early return AFTER all hooks
  if (!project || !activeTabId || !activeTab) return null;
  if (activeTab.commandType !== 'gemini') return null;
  if (subAgentTabs.length === 0) return null;

  return (
    <div
      className="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-2 border-b border-border-main"
      style={{
        height: '28px',
        backgroundColor: 'rgba(30, 30, 30, 0.95)',
        fontSize: '11px',
      }}
    >
      {/* Fixed-width label that toggles between "Sub-agents:" and "← Back" — no layout shift */}
      <button
        onClick={handleLabelClick}
        className="flex items-center rounded transition-colors shrink-0"
        style={{
          fontSize: '10px',
          color: viewingSubAgentTabId ? 'rgba(255,255,255,0.6)' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.35)',
          cursor: viewingSubAgentTabId ? 'pointer' : 'default',
          minWidth: '68px',
          background: viewingSubAgentTabId ? 'rgba(255,255,255,0.05)' : 'transparent',
          padding: '2px 6px',
        }}
      >
        {viewingSubAgentTabId ? '← Back' : 'Sub-agents:'}
      </button>

      {subAgentTabs.map((tab, i) => {
        const isViewing = viewingSubAgentTabId === tab.id;
        const isRunning = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'running' || (!tab.claudeAgentStatus && tab.claudeSessionId);
        const isDone = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'done';
        const isError = tab.claudeAgentStatus === 'error';

        let indicatorColor = '#DA7756';
        if (isDone) indicatorColor = '#a6e3a1';
        if (isError) indicatorColor = '#f38ba8';

        return (
          <button
            key={tab.id}
            onClick={() => handleChipClick(tab.id)}
            onContextMenu={(e) => handleDetach(e, tab.id)}
            className="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-2 py-0.5 rounded transition-colors"
            style={{
              backgroundColor: isViewing ? 'rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.3)' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.06)',
              border: isViewing ? '1px solid rgba(204, 120, 50, 0.5)' : '1px solid transparent',
              color: isViewing ? '#cc7832' : 'rgba(255,255,255,0.7)',
              cursor: 'pointer',
            }}
            title="Click to view, right-click to detach"
          >
            {/* Square indicator instead of robot emoji */}
            <span
              style={{
                display: 'inline-block',
                width: '7px',
                height: '7px',
                borderRadius: '2px',
                backgroundColor: indicatorColor,
                boxShadow: isRunning ? `0 0 6px ${indicatorColor}80` : 'none',
                animation: isRunning ? 'subagent-pulse 1.5s ease-in-out infinite' : 'none',
              }}
            />
            <span>Claude #{i + 1}</span>
            {isDone && <span style={{ color: '#a6e3a1', fontSize: '10px' }}>✓</span>}
            {isError && <span style={{ color: '#f38ba8', fontSize: '10px' }}>✗</span>}
          </button>
        );
      })}

      {/* Inline keyframes for pulse animation */}
      <style>{`
        @keyframes subagent-pulse {
          0%, 100% { opacity: 1; }
          50% { opacity: 0.35; }
        }
      `}</style>
    </div>
  );
}
```

- Write a quick E2E test that sends a "think hard" prompt to Claude and captures/logs the raw PTY output to understand the ANSI patterns
- Analyze what we can detect from the terminal output

The existing state machine already tracks IDLE → BUSY transitions based on prompt detection, so I could apply a similar approach to detect thinking state. The spinner characters Claude outputs while thinking have specific ANSI color codes, so if I can identify those patterns in the PTY data stream, I can set a thinking flag independently from the general process state.

For the investigation, I'll create a test script that launches Claude, sends a complex prompt, and logs the raw PTY output so I can identify the thinking patterns.

The user wants me to run an E2E test first to capture what Claude's thinking output actually looks like, then build a plan from there. (thinking)` with Unicode spinner characters and ANSI colors, and the existing PTY middleware already tracks IDLE/BUSY transitions when the prompt disappears and output starts flowing.

But for the TabBar indicator, there's a complication: Claude doesn't emit OSC 133 shell integration events like regular commands do, so I need to track Claude-specific state using the `commandType === 'claude'` flag and `claudeSessionId` that we're already capturing.
